<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:322px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">sets  (big- data)  and  complex  mathematical  models  that  track  hundreds  of  ecological

<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:351px; width:100px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:4px">4</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:7px">Science Partners, Paris, France

<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:367px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">models that need to be integrated over long time- scales to simulate the distribution 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:382px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">of ecosystems carbon and nutrient pools and fluxes. Here, we introduce a machine- 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:397px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">learning acceleration (MLA) tool to tackle this grand challenge. We focus on the most 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:412px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">resource- consuming step in terrestrial biosphere models (TBMs): the equilibration of 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:427px; width:339px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">biogeochemical cycles (spin- up), a prerequisite that can take up to 98% of the com-
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:442px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">putational time. Through three members of the ORCHIDEE TBM family part of the 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:457px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">IPSL Earth System Model, including versions that describe the complex interactions 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:472px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">between nitrogen, phosphorus and carbon that do not have any analytical solution for 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:487px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">the spin- up, we show that an unoptimized MLA reduced the computation demand by 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:502px; width:339px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">77%– 80% for global studies via interpolating the equilibrated state of biogeochemi-
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:517px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">cal  variables  for  a  subset  of  model  pixels.  Despite  small  biases  in  the  MLA- derived 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:532px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">equilibrium, the resulting impact on the predicted regional carbon balance over recent 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:547px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">decades is minor. We expect a one- order of magnitude lower computation demand 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:562px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">by optimizing the choices of machine learning algorithms, their settings, and balancing 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:577px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">the trade- off between quality of MLA predictions and need for TBM simulations for 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:592px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">training data generation and bias reduction. Our tool is agnostic to gridded models 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:607px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">(beyond TBMs), compatible with existing spin- up acceleration procedures, and opens 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:622px; width:341px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">the  door  to  a  wide  variety  of  future  applications,  with  complex  non- linear  models 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:203px; top:637px; width:191px; height:9px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:9px">benefit most from the computational efficiency.

<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:1312px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">requires up to 10,000 model years to reach a steady- state for carbon 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:1311px; width:235px; height:10px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Bold; font-size:10px">2.1  </span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:10px">|</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Bold; font-size:10px">  ML- based procedure for accelerated spin- up

<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:1351px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">span  only  a  few  100 years  (e.g.  the  historical  period  1700– present

<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:1377px; width:242px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">ing  conventional  spin- up  for  the  selected  training  pixels;  (3)  build-

<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:1416px; width:242px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">usually model specific, and they rely largely on linearity to approx-

<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:1429px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">imate  analytical  solutions  and  become  inefficient  with  increasing

<br/>et al.,  2018), and Global Carbon Budget: Land modeling protocol

<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:3497px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">We used three versions of the ORCHIDEE model: ORCHIDEE (v2.2) the

<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:3536px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">according  to  the  abovementioned  protocols  (Table  3).  Simulations 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:3549px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">et al., 2017), and ORCHIDEE- CNP v1.3 an update of the branch version 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:3549px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">prescribing constant boundary conditions for the initial year (1700 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:3562px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">which resolves non- linear microbial dynamics instead of deploying a linear 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:3562px; width:242px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">or 1860), and simulations with varying boundary conditions reflect-
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:3575px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">first order decay model like the other two versions (Goll et al., 2022; Table 2). 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:3575px; width:242px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">ing  their  changes  over  the  historic  period.  The  first  type  of  simu-
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:3588px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">The three versions reflect the general tendency in the TBM community to 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:3588px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">lations  is  needed  to  generate  the  training  information  for  the  ML 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:3601px; width:242px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">refine processes operating on various timescales: for example, microbial dy-

<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:3614px; width:242px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">namics on timescales of minutes to months, while soil phosphorus dynam-
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:3614px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">scratch (low globally uniform values) to derive the transient states 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:3627px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">ics on timescales up to thousands of years. The number of state variables 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:3640px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">describing the biogeochemical cycles in soil, litter and plants depends on the 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:3627px; width:244px; height:21px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">of  NPP</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:5px">g</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">,  LAI</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:5px">g</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">,  as  well  as  pixel  level  conventional  TBM  simulations 
<br/>for  the  selected  representative  model  pixels  starting  from  scratch 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:3653px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">model version and ranges between 240 and 825 (Table 2; Data S3). All three 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:3653px; width:242px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">to  steady  state  (see  Section  2.3)  in  which  the  biogeochemical  cy-
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:3666px; width:242px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">versions deploy a tiling approach in which each model pixel contains infor-
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:3666px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">cles  were  equilibrated  (</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">site- runs</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">).  The  second  type  of  simulation  is 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:3679px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">mation on biogeochemical cycles of multiple PFTs (each PFT has a specific

<br/>(i.e. annual changes in global land carbon storage are </span><span style="font-family: STIX-Regular; font-size:8px">&lt;</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">0.05 Gt year</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:5px">−1</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">
<br/>when averaged over a 50 year period; Friedlingstein et al., 2022). To

<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:4355px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">which requires information from multiple model pixels at a time. The

<br/>(Figures 2– 4, Figures S3– S6). The slopes are commonly lower than

<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:5582px; width:503px; height:85px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Bold; font-size:8px">F I G U R E   2</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px"> The performances of machine learning models (ML) on all carbon cycle state variables, with the sum of state variables of major 
<br/>biosphere compartment ((a,d,g) soil organic carbon (SOC), (b,e,h) biomass, and (c,f,i) litter) for each plant functional type compared to the 
<br/>‘true equilibrium’ of the conventional spin- up simulation (</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">spin- up</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:5px">conv</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">). Three statistics represent the model performance: (a–c) coefficient of 
<br/>determination (</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">R</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:5px">2</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">), (d–f) normalized root mean squared error (NRMSE), and (g–i) the regression slope between the results from ML and  
<br/> </span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">spin- up</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:5px">conv</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px"> (slope). Shown are results from ORCHIDEE- CNP v1.3. The plant functional types are: Tropical Evergreen Broadleaf Forest (TrEBF), 
<br/>Tropical Deciduous Broadleaf Forest (TrDBF), Temperate Evergreen Needleleaf Forest (TeENF), Temperate Evergreen Broadleaf forest 
<br/>(TeEBF), Temperate Deciduous Broadleaf Forest (TeDBF), Boreal Evergreen Needleleaf Forest (BoENF), Boreal Deciduous Broadleaf Forest 
<br/>(BoDBF), Boreal Deciduous Needleleaf Forest (BoDNF), C3 grassland (C3G), C4 grassland (C4G), C3 cropland (C3C), and C4 cropland (C4C).
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:5695px; width:244px; height:21px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">The  procedure  works  best  for  the  carbon  only  model  version 
<br/></span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">with the majority of </span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">R</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:5px">2</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px"> above 0.9, slopes between 0.9 and 1.0, and 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:5695px; width:244px; height:21px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">steady- state in the </span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">site- runs</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px"> and </span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">spin- up</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:5px">conv</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px"> than in other two model 
<br/></span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">versions (not shown). This is due to the chosen equilibrium criteria 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:5721px; width:244px; height:21px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">NRMSE</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px"> smaller than 0.1 (Figure S6). The quality of ML predictions is 
<br/>the lowest for ORCHIDEE- CNP v1.2 with </span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">R</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:5px">2</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px"> as lower than 0.7 for 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:5721px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">which focus on global C stocks rather than on pixel- level ones (see 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:5734px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">Section 2) and is thus insufficient to ensure that (1) state variables 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:5747px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">46% of all C state variables at PFT- level (Figures S3– S5). This is likely 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:5747px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">of all model pixels are at equilibration, (2) the nutrient cycles are in 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:5760px; width:244px; height:7px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:7px">due to the fact a larger number of model pixels has not yet reached a 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:5760px; width:42px; height:7px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:7px">equilibrium.

<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9374px; width:211px; height:23px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:10px">3.6.2  |  Towards the improved assimilation of 
<br/>observations into TBMs
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9415px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">TBMs have been criticized regarding their reliability, primarily because 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9428px; width:242px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">of a large number of unconstrained model parameters. The applica-
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9441px; width:242px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">tions  of  model- data  fusion  (or  data  assimilation)  for  TBMs  are  ham-
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9454px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">pered by the computational bottleneck, with measurements of carbon 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9467px; width:242px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">stocks seldom being systematically assimilated to improve parameteri-
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9480px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">zation (MacBean et al., 2022). Instead, parameters that control short- 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9493px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">term processes are optimized assuming that long- term processes have 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9506px; width:242px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">limited  impacts  on  short- term  dynamics.  While  this  assumption,  im-
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9519px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">posed  by  the  computational  cost,  facilitates  specific  applications,  it 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9532px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">is inadequate to solve the parameterization challenge for TBMs with 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9545px; width:242px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">multiple interactive processes with various timescales in their evolu-
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9558px; width:244px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">tion. The elimination of the computational bottleneck through MLA is 
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:306px; top:9571px; width:191px; height:8px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">an essential step toward systematic model- data fusion.
<br/></span></div><div style="position:absolute; border: textbox 1px solid; writing-mode:lr-tb; left:45px; top:9485px; width:243px; height:96px;"><span style="font-family: Lato-Bold; font-size:8px">F I G U R E   7</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px"> The computational demand of the historical simulation 
<br/>type (</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">production- run</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:5px">MLA</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px"> or </span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">production- run</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:5px">conv</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">) and the MLA based 
<br/>spin- up (consisting of </span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">pre- run</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">, </span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">site- run</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:5px">MLA</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">, and </span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">re- run</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">) as percentage 
<br/>of the demand of the conventional spin- up type (</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:8px">spin- up</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Italic; font-size:5px">conv</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px">) for three 
<br/>versions of the ORCHIDEE family. In the case of ORCHIDEE v2.2 we 
<br/>show the computational demands when the version- specific spin- up 
<br/>acceleration procedure was activated (ORC v2.2, specific </span><span style="font-family: STIX-Regular; font-size:8px">+</span><span style="font-family: Lato-Regular; font-size:8px"> MLA) 
<br/>or not (ORC v2.2*, MLA- only). ORC v2.2 shows computation time 
<br/>relative to the version- specific spin- up acceleration procedure.
